Track and Field General Review

The track and field events were completed yesterday. Looking at the results of the two days, the shot put and 10,000-meter race results were excellent. The 800-meter and 100-meter were also not weak. Wang Jihuai's first place in the pentathlon was quite good, and the decathlon was also remarkable. Although the women's results were not excellent, it is commendable that they participated in the competition and had a martial spirit. Overall, the results were quite average. Although the weather was not warm and it had rained for several days, they had not had sufficient practice, but the results were already impressive. If they undergo careful training for another ten days, they can attend the National Games and compete with the Liaoning athletes. If they cannot win the championship, they can certainly secure the second place. I hope our male and female athletes will strive for it. Below is a record of Mr. Gao's comments:

In the 100-meter final, Chen Baoqiu had the fastest start, but in terms of style and pace, Zhong Lianji was the best. He steadily gained ground, and reached 50 meters alongside Chen. His speed increased even more afterward, and he reached the finish line as the first person. The old general on the field was indeed extraordinary.

In the women's 50-meter, Liu Jingfang's results in the preliminary and semi-final were particularly good, like a crane standing among chickens. However, in yesterday's final, she had a late start, lagging behind the others by two steps. It was not easy for her to rise quickly and catch up to second place in a very short distance.

Wang Jianwu is a veteran in the 400-meter race. Ten years ago, he achieved unique results in the Jiangsu Provincial Games. Although he is now working for an electric company, he still participates in sports and often stands out in Shanghai's public sports events. In yesterday's 400-meter final, Wang took the lead at the start and led the crowd until 50 meters. He continued to work hard afterwards, without any slackening. In the eyes of the public, he was already considered the first person. Unexpectedly, there was a sudden change, and Su Zuqing rushed out in the last ten meters, which was very unfortunate. However, Su was also very brave.

In the high hurdles final, the competition between Li Jingbang and Cao Yu was extremely fierce, and the difference in results was very slight. Before the fourth hurdle, Li was in front, and Cao followed closely. By the eighth hurdle, Cao jumped to the front. At this time, Li certainly worked hard to decide the final outcome. When crossing the last hurdle, the two jumped and landed at the same time without any difference. However, in the 15-meter sprint, Cao, having consumed too much energy from competing in the decathlon, was relatively inferior and lagged behind by half a step, finishing second.

In the women's baseball throw, Fan Ruimei's method was appropriate, and her strength was sufficient. She threw six times, all beyond 70 meters, which amazed the spectators. After the competition, a certain referee tried to throw the ball once, but was ashamed of being inferior.

Among the various competitions, the one that could arouse the audience's keenest interest was the 10,000-meter final. A large group of athletes ran bravely, circling the field twenty-five times, which was a wonderful spectacle. Moreover, Sun Qin, one of them, was funny and quirky. Every time he passed the stand, he would change to a unique posture, either bending his waist or stretching his arms, or leaping lightly like dancing or running straight like a ... The spectators laughed when they saw it. Long-distance runner Chen Xuzhou had light and agile footsteps, always leading the way. Dong Jiaxie, a Tongji school warrior, also strode very naturally, and often ranked second after three laps without being hurried. In the last lap, Zhou Bin suddenly chased out, presumably because Zhou had reserved his strength for later.

Yesterday's Basketball Results

Six Stars Won the Women's Basketball Championship

—Defeated Southeast 22 to 15 Yesterday—

Liangjiang Forfeited the Day Before Yesterday

Six Stars Won 2 to 0

The Six Stars Women's Basketball Team played against the Southeast Women's Physical Education School Basketball Team at the China Basketball Hall starting at 5 PM yesterday. The Six Stars' basketball skills were no longer what they used to be, and Southeast was once a well-known strong team. Both sides were extremely strong, and the competition was very fierce. As a result, Six Stars overcame Southeast with an excellent performance, won the championship of this City Games, and won the championship, which is deeply gratifying. The result was 22 to 15, referee Song Junfu.

Liangjiang Forfeited

In the game between Liangjiang and Six Stars the day before yesterday, Liangjiang won. However, Liangjiang player Xi Jun had served as a physical education teacher at Chengdong Women's School last year, and her qualifications did not meet the requirements. Yesterday morning, the organizing committee sent someone to the school to inquire and confirmed that Ms. Xi was responsible for morning exercises in the Chinese painting class, as well as one hour each of gymnastics and music in the other classes. Therefore, the result of that game was deemed a forfeit for Liangjiang, and Six Stars won 2 to 0.

Six Stars is Formidable

The Six Stars' performance last night was better than ever, because the battle line had been slightly changed. Chen Xinyuan was transferred to center, and Zhu Minbao replaced Lu Yao. Although Liang Lifang was a strong rear guard, what could she do? Chen Xinyuan is the best among the three forwards, Chen Yingrui is the fastest, and Zhu Minbao is still satisfactory. If they had used this lineup to fight Liangjiang earlier, they might have overcome them sooner, so why wait for Liangjiang to forfeit? Apart from Liang's younger sister being slightly weaker among the three rear guards, what more can be said about Ye Fuji and Yu Qiying?

Southeast is Diminished

Since winning the China Association Championship, Southeast has only had two wonderful performances at the beginning of the West Qing Competition. Since then, there have been no remarkable matches. After forfeiting in the West Qing Competition, its prestige was greatly reduced. Therefore, Six Stars came with a determination to win, and after the clash, they immediately saw that Southeast was no match for them. The difference was far too great. They could not attack and their defense was also very difficult. Among the forwards, Dun Xiaoping could not support the building alone. Apart from Jiang Huaixuan, there is little praise to be given to the rear guards. They were subdued by Six Stars from beginning to end.

Men's Basketball Semi-Finals

East-West and Green Light Gain Final Rights

East-West Wins Over Tongji: 33-25

Green Light Wins Over Chih-Chih: 30-26

The basketball semi-finals were held last night, with two groups in total. The matches started at 6 PM at the Chinese Basketball Hall. As a result, East-West won over Tongji with 33-25, and Green Light defeated Chih-Chih with 30-26. Thus, East-West and Green Light obtained the final rights. The intense battle situations of the two groups are recorded as follows:

East-West Turns Defeat into Victory

In the initial expectations for the East-West versus Tongji match, it was supposed to be a one-sided game.

Chen Chong, the forward, and Lu Zhong'en also sat out to rest. When the two teams met, Tongji surprisingly advanced like a broken bamboo. Starting with Meng Jixian scoring the first point with Hou Zhi's foul penalty, they continued to increase the score. Tongji reached 14 points, while East-West had not yet opened the score. Lu then entered the game, and the momentum was still good. East-West tried once but failed, and the ball ultimately did not enter the basket. Tongji greatly won the first half with 18-7. At this point, Huang Yunli,

and Liang Guoquan had to enter the game. With excellent passing, Chen Xianglong frequently scored consecutive hits, and the score was tied after five minutes. Tongji then collapsed. East-West thus turned defeat into victory. Fortunately, the final score was 33-25. The referee was Xu Zhendong.

Green Light Obtains Final Rights

The battle between Green Light and Chih-Chih was extremely tense. The scores of the two teams differed only by one or two points each time. Although Green Light was strong, Chih-Chih was not weak either, so the outcome could not be immediately determined. Chi Zhi's Zeng Guangrong opened the scoring first. By the end of the first half, it was 14-9. Lemon restarted the battle. Although Chih-Chih tried hard to catch up, they were unable to do so. Green Light's defender, Kong Guangyi, repeatedly scored long shots. Thus, Chih-Chih consistently lagged behind by three or four points. As a result, the score was 30-26, and Green Light won. The referee was Zhang Guozhu.

The Unexpectedly Rising Feixing Team

The patriotic girls' school in this city has long been renowned on the sea. Its liberal arts and sports departments, judging from past history, have collected the elites from the boudoirs of the north and south of the Yangtze River. The liberal arts students are good at dominating the literary world, while the sports students are mostly lively individuals who compete in the martial arena. However, this time, they participated in the city's sports meet, breaking the previous example. The so-called unexpectedly rising Feixing team is organized by a mix of liberal arts and sports students. Writers who appreciate the scenery of Lake Feng also participate in it. The spirit of this team is said to be extremely perfect, containing both heroic and refined talents. The team's idea is to fully develop their talents and fight to the end. Therefore, even though there are experienced and strong enemies in front of them in this city, they resolutely joined. It has now been decided that they will compete against the Minli team this afternoon. People still do not know where Feixing came from, so this article is specially written to describe its brief history and the origin of the Feixing team.

[P Jiangsu Provincial Games to Open Today>

The Venue is in Zhenjiang, and Provincial School Games will be Held First for Three Days

Starting from the 18th, a Preliminary Meeting of the Public will be Held to Select Representatives

The opening ceremony of the third Jiangsu Provincial Games and the Provincial Secondary School Games will be held today (the 15th) morning. The venue is the large drill ground outside the South Gate of Zhenjiang, which is quiet, remote, and spacious, making it a rare venue in the local area. The Games will last for three days, until the 17th. From the 18th to the 10th, the Jiangsu Provincial Public Preliminary Meeting for the National Games will be held. The scale of both events is grand, and the number of athletes is large, making it a glorious record in the history of Jiangsu sports.

The Central School Games has a two-year history of excellence. This year is the third session. The first session was the Jiangsu University District, renamed the Central University District last year, and this session has been renamed again. The sports events include only track and field, divided into male A and B groups and a female group. There will also be group performances and a ball game championship. This year, the Games will be temporarily missing and replaced by a public preliminary meeting. Participating schools include 39 for males and 8 for females, with 401 male athletes and 86 female athletes. At that time, they will show their skills in the grand arena, which will surely cause a sensation in Zhenjiang. The various situations are recorded separately below:

Abolish Winter Vacation and Extend New Year Vacation

The Ministry of Education will issue an order.

According to various requests, the Ministry of Education will abolish winter vacation and extend New Year vacation. It had submitted a request to the Executive Yuan, which was then forwarded to the National Government. The National Government has now approved the filing and instructed the Ministry of Education to comply. It is heard that the main points of the reasons advocated for this are: (1) In the past, winter vacation was mostly during the lunar calendar, close to the end of the year. Now that the lunar calendar has been abolished, if the winter vacation is not changed, the schools will be on vacation during the lunar New Year, which would be contrary to the purpose of advocating the national calendar. Now, the name of winter vacation is avoided, and the New Year vacation is extended, with the vacation taking place during the Gregorian New Year, in order to correct the hidden practice of taking lunar New Year vacations. (2) In the past, the two semesters each year were very different in length. To adjust the average length of the two semesters, winter vacation is abolished and New Year vacation is extended. It is heard that the National Government considers the various points submitted by the Ministry of Education to be quite reasonable and has therefore approved them. The detailed measures will be announced by the Ministry of Education.

Supervisor of Students Studying in Japan Takes Office Yesterday

Wang Keming, the newly appointed supervisor of students studying in Japan by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, came to Shanghai a few days ago after receiving his appointment to pack his luggage and bid farewell to relatives and friends from all directions. He then took the Japanese ship Nagasaki Maru to Yokohama yesterday afternoon. He also sent a letter to the Japanese Ambassador to China, Shigemitsu Mamoru, as well as to the director of the Yokohama Customs, requesting that Wang's luggage be exempted from inspection upon arrival and allowed to pass.

Continued Sino-Japanese Commercial Treaty Negotiations in Shanghai

British Envoy Expected to Arrive in Beijing Within a Week

Nepalese Intrusion into Tibet Under Investigation

Mutual Benefit Opposition Explained by Finance Minister Song

——Conversation with Wang Zhengting——

This newspaper's reporter met with Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting yesterday to inquire about various diplomatic news. The following is a summary of his remarks: Regarding the Sino-Japanese commercial treaty, Mr. Wang stated that the Sino-Japanese tariff agreement had already been signed in draft form, so the tariff portion of the Sino-Japanese commercial treaty could be considered concluded. Negotiations will continue on the abolition of extraterritoriality and navigation rights. Regarding navigation rights, he will consult with Minister of Communications Wang Boqun on all related matters. It is expected that a complete resolution of the Sino-Japanese commercial treaty will not be far off. During this visit to Shanghai, he also plans to meet with Japanese Acting Minister Shigemitsu to begin negotiations, but the date has not been set. He may be able to meet today if time permits. The reporter asked whether the Minister had read the telegram from the National Federation of Commerce opposing Sino-Japanese tariff reciprocity. Mr. Wang replied that the National Federation of Commerce was mistaken. The agreement reached was not for reciprocal tariffs at all. He will ask Finance Minister Song Ziwen to explain it to the chamber of commerce in detail.

Regarding Sino-French negotiations, the reporter inquired about recent developments in the Sino-French Vietnam commercial treaty negotiations. Mr. Wang said that the French are most adept at changing their minds. Although Director Hu Shize is in Beiping liaising with the French envoy, there have been no new developments. The note regarding the recovery of the French Concession in Shanghai has not yet been issued.

Regarding the British envoy's visit to Beijing, the National Government has formally appointed Wang Zhengting as the plenipotentiary representative for negotiating the special treaty on the recovery of Weihaiwei. The reporter asked when the British envoy would arrive in Beijing to begin negotiations. Mr. Wang said that British Envoy Lampson would arrive in Beijing within a week to meet with him. The Weihaiwei recovery issue is expected to be resolved soon.

Regarding the investigation of Tibetan affairs, the reporter also inquired about the Panchen Lama's representative in Beijing, Losang Jianzan, who had presented a petition to the National Government stating that Nepal was launching a large-scale attack on Tibet and requesting that measures be taken to prevent it. He asked whether the Ministry of Foreign Affairs was prepared for this. Mr. Wang replied that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs had telegraphed all parties to investigate the true situation regarding the Nepalese intrusion into Tibet. A special commissioner will be dispatched to Tibet to inspect the situation and provide a factual basis for further action.

Wang Zhengting Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

Luncheon to be Held Today to Welcome Canadian Envoy and Wife

Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting and his wife arrived in Shanghai by express train from Beijing yesterday morning, reaching the port at 5:40 PM yesterday afternoon. That evening, they attended the British Consul-General Sir Barton's banquet at the Da Hua Hotel in honor of Canadian Minister to Japan, Mr. and Mrs. Marler. At 1:00 PM today, Mr. and Mrs. Wang will host a banquet at the Diplomatic Discussion Society to welcome Mr. and Mrs. Marler. Those invited to attend include Mr. and Mrs. Cunningham, the American Consul-General, Mr. and Mrs. Sir Barton, the British Consul-General, and Mr. and Mrs. Chu Minyi, totaling about twenty people. Tonight, the Canadian Trade Commissioner in Shanghai will host a banquet at the Da Hua Hotel, which Mr. and Mrs. Wang and members of the diplomatic community will attend.

Japanese Acting Minister Returned to Shanghai Yesterday Morning

Japanese Acting Minister Shigemitsu Aoi, having completed his official duties in Beijing, returned to Shanghai by night train with Secretary Hayashi and Secretary Asaka the night before last, arriving in Shanghai at 7:00 AM yesterday (the 14th). He went to his private residence on Seymour Road to rest, and then went to the office as usual to work. According to news from the Japanese Consulate, the Sino-Japanese tariff issue has been resolved. Mr. Shigemitsu is eager to negotiate the second major issue in the Sino-Japanese treaty, namely the issue of extraterritoriality. He has already discussed the matter with Foreign Minister Wang at a banquet in Beijing and has begun to explore the matter. Mr. Uemura, the Japanese consul stationed in Beijing who is researching this issue, and Mr. Shimizu, the consul stationed in Shanghai, have both been ordered to prepare everything. It is planned that when Foreign Minister Wang visits Shanghai next time, formal talks will be held on this matter. It is expected that negotiations will be completed within two months and a draft agreement will be signed. Other issues, such as inland navigation rights, will also be negotiated in turn. All major issues in the new Sino-Japanese treaty are to be resolved within this year.

Japanese Commercial Officer Yokotake Returned to His Country

After the signing of the draft Sino-Japanese tariff agreement, Foreign Minister Wang presented it to the National Government for review, while Japanese Acting Minister Shigemitsu Aoi ordered the commercial attache of the embassy, Yokotake, to take the draft back to his country to report to the Japanese government on the progress of the negotiations and request approval of the agreement for formal signing. Commercial Officer Yokotake, having received the order, returned to his country yesterday morning on the Nagasaki Maru mail ship. The Nagasaki Maru mail ship, due to encountering a storm, only entered the port yesterday morning and did not depart until 11:00 AM. Consul Miura and Secretary Horiuchi went to the port to see him off.

Yang Shuzhuang Arrived in Shanghai

May Arrive in Song Late Last Night or This Morning

According to news from the Naval Reorganization Office yesterday, Minister Yang Shuzhuang left Mawei on the Puan warship at 8:00 AM on the 13th to come to Shanghai. Those traveling with him included Secretary Wu Shan and Adjutant Jiang Zhizhuang. Commander Chen Jiliang remained in Fujian to oversee the situation. Whether members of the provincial government were on board was not mentioned. The Puan warship could have arrived at the Songkou port around 10:00 PM, but due to mechanical damage en route, it traveled very slowly and will not arrive until after 12:00 AM. The Reorganization Office, led by Bureau Chief Ren Guangyu and Adjutant Wang Shuheng of the Military Affairs Bureau, boarded a Jiangnan tugboat at 5:00 PM yesterday evening and sailed to Songkou to welcome him. Mr. Yang disembarked at the Wusong Customs Wharf, while the Puan warship will sail to Gaochang Temple for repairs by the Jiangnan Shipyard. It is also heard that although Cheng Shih-gui and two others have been transferred to the province, there is no news of the transfer of Lin Zhiyuan and two others.

US Asiatic Fleet Commander, Vice Admiral McVay, Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

Wenhui Daily reports that US Asiatic Fleet Commander, Vice Admiral McVay, arrived in Shanghai on his flagship, the Pittsburgh, from the Philippines at 11:45 AM today (the 14th). It is said that the ship will remain in Shanghai until mid-June, before proceeding to Qingdao. It is also heard that the Pittsburgh is old and will be replaced by the newly built cruiser Houston in September.

Large Sum of Foreign Currency Arrived in Shanghai

50 Million in Foreign Currency Imported

Since the sharp rise in gold prices and the fall in silver prices, the influx of foreign silver into China has continued unabated. Large bars of silver from San Francisco and New York are imported every time a Pacific mail ship arrives in Shanghai (an average of seven times a month), resulting in a large silver surplus in Shanghai. It is also heard that another batch will be imported next Monday. However, at a time when gold and silver prices are fluctuating and people are panicking, a large number of silver coins from India and Annam have suddenly been transported to Shanghai, totaling 50 million yuan. In the most recent period, three batches have already been loaded, totaling 4.75 million boxes, or about 23 million yuan. The fourth shipment of foreign currency is expected to arrive next Monday, with approximately 7 million yuan arriving that day. The remaining 20 million yuan is scheduled to be loaded and shipped to Shanghai within four weeks. This huge amount of foreign currency was purchased by a certain foreign bank in Shanghai, and its purpose is unclear. It is said that it will be melted into silver bars in China and then used in our country to reap huge profits.

Chamber of Commerce Condemns Yan and Feng by Telegram

Love the Country, Not Personal Gain

On the 10th of this month, the Chamber of Commerce received a telegram jointly signed by Yan Xishan and Feng Yuxiang, which stated in brief that the purpose of establishing chambers of commerce is to supervise the actions of merchants, guide them into the right path, and thereby maintain the peace and tranquility of the country and society. Therefore, chambers of commerce are heavily responsible to the people. In recent years, the Shanghai banking and money exchange associations have borrowed and raised debts, providing funds on a daily basis. Public opinion generally points out that the chamber of commerce has neither heard the legitimate demands of representing the people, nor been able to effectively supervise the two associations. Justice is not upheld, legal rights are abandoned, and the responsibility to the people is minimal. After receiving the telegram, the Chamber of Commerce decided at its regular executive meeting yesterday to reply by telegram. The full text is as follows: "To Mr. Yan Xichuan and Mr. Feng Huanzhang in Taiyuan, upon reading your esteemed telegram, we were bewildered and perplexed, and suspected it was untrue due to the distance and remoteness. Since the establishment of the Republic of China, for more than ten years, warlord autocracy has led to successive disasters. We were fortunate that the revolution was successful and there was hope for recovery. After unification, reorganization and disbandment followed, military tensions were eliminated, and construction was urgently needed. The merchants of the whole country eagerly looked forward to governance. They spared no effort to contribute their humble efforts and actively promote the issuance of various government bonds and treasury bills by the central government. All they hoped for was to consolidate the national foundation, achieve unification, reduce military expenditure, and maintain lasting peace. They loved the country, not for personal gain. Moreover, in terms of the timing of the issuance of government bonds, except for the customs and reorganization treasury bills, the rest were all before May of the 18th year of the Republic. At that time, Huan Gong was the Vice President of the Executive Yuan. Even after the issuance of the customs and reorganization treasury bills, Lu Zhonglin still took office as the Minister of Military Affairs on August 19th, and on August 24th of the same month, the Third Reorganization District Reorganization Conference was held in Taiyuan. Moreover, Bai Gong recently took office as Deputy Commander, also speaking of implementing reorganization and carrying out peace. The merchants only saw the military authorities engaging in reorganization, and the telegrams and meetings had both words and deeds. They believed that years of longing would be fulfilled in one day. They did not hesitate to transfer their trade and sweat-earned capital to help the major plan of saving the country. If this is their crime, what else can be said? If it is said that the successive bonds should not have been issued, then the two associations once held important positions in the central government and did not hear of any corrections. To know but not speak is disloyal, to not know and not speak is dereliction of duty. The people should have accusations against the two associations, but the two associations instead consider the merchants guilty. Judging from the situation and reasoning, how can this be fair? We have the following suggestion: in the disaster areas of the Northwest, deaths are occurring on the road; in the Southeast, the financial resources are exhausted. The people are like those who have been sick and have undergone surgery several times. At this time, they can only rest quietly to recover their vitality. As for how clothes can fit the body and what kind of food is most nourishing, these are all idle talks that do not help save lives. Just as Bai Gong advised Huan Gong in his telegram on June 10th of the 18th year of the Republic, we must not allow the people in the disaster areas to suffer another catastrophe. The two associations are enlightened and should consider this early. Political disputes have their own rules, and public opinion is the final force. We respectfully send this telegram to express our opinion fully. If you can examine it carefully, we would be greatly honored. The Shanghai Special Municipality Merchant Association Reorganization Committee bows. Cold."

Commercial Ship Accident Report

Collision Between Chinese and Japanese Merchant Ships

The Nanhua liner Lushan Maru, of the Nisshin Kisen Kaisha, transported passengers from the stranded Balu Maru at Nanao Island, east of Shantou, to Guangdong and other places. It then carried cargo and passengers from Guangdong and Xiamen back to Shanghai. It entered the port at 10:00 AM yesterday. When the ship arrived at the Huangpu River and docked at the Nisshin Kisen pier in Pudong, it needed to turn around. At the same time, the Longshan, of the Sanpei Company, which was transporting coal from Qingdao to Shanghai, also entered the port at 10:30 AM and intended to go to the Hongan pier in Pudong to unload. However, when the ship passed in front of the Yitaixing pier, it was sailing south and had just passed the Nisshin Kisen pier when the Lushan Maru turned. The stern of the Lushan Maru protruded horizontally into the river. The captain of the Longshan saw it and hurriedly steered to avoid it, but it was too late. The stern of the Longshan collided violently with the stern of the Lushan Maru. The rudder and stern iron plates of the Longshan were damaged, and the cabins on the stern deck of the Lushan Maru were also destroyed. Fortunately, no one was injured. This occurred around 12:00 PM. The two ships docked at the pier, and the shipowners of Sanpei and Nisshin Kisen each sent representatives to inspect the damage and make repairs first, so as not to hinder the export schedule. There are now nine cases of damage to various large and small boats that have been reported to the water police station for record, and there are many more that have not been reported. The reported cases are listed below: (1) Xu Qilang's pier boat, carrying 340 barrels of indigo for the Yongfengli customs broker, the boat and cargo sank to the bottom of the Huangpu River; (2) A certain pier boat, also carrying 360 barrels for the Yongfengli customs broker, the boat and cargo sank to the bottom of the Huangpu River; (3) Sun Hongqing's rural boat, carrying 21 tons of coal, the boat and cargo sank completely; (4) Peng Fudongzi's pier boat, the corner of the boat was damaged; (5) Han Xiaosizi's pier boat, carrying 320 bags of flour, the boat and cargo sank completely; (6) Xiang Jinli's empty pier boat, sank to the bottom of the Huangpu River; (7) Shen Shunliang's rural boat, the hull was damaged; (8) Bao Axiu's pier boat, carrying 100 pieces of foreign fabrics, the boat and cargo sank completely; (9) Kang Donghai's pier boat, carrying 44 tons of coal, the boat and cargo sank to the bottom of the Huangpu River.

Huangpu Steamer Collides with Pier

The Taikoo Company's Huangpu steamer arrived in Shanghai from Hankou at around 11:00 AM yesterday. Due to the strong wind and rapid tide at that time, it sailed south along the Pudong side and intended to turn around upstream of the Huangpu River. When it sailed to the Yangjiadu China Merchants Warehouse Pier, because the hull was too close to the shore and was impacted by the wind and water, the hull crashed into the pier, instantly damaging several pier boats, and the bow continued to advance, crashing into the warehouse pier, causing severe damage. After trying to tow the ship outwards, it returned to the company's pier and docked.

Zhengji Steamer Disaster News

This port received a telegram from Tianjin yesterday, stating that on the 2nd of this month, a Zhengji steamer arrived in Tianjin from Tanggu Port. In the Baihe River, due to careless navigation, it collided with and sank many ferry boats and cargo barges. Many boatmen fell into the water and died. The shipowner is Japanese, and it is heard that the Tianjin authorities have detained the shipowner and will punish him for dereliction of duty.

Chamber of Commerce Suggests to Fessenden

Eleven Improvements Needed for Concession Municipality

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce for All Roads, because the Shanghai Municipal Council has issued a notice soliciting opinions from Chinese organizations and individuals regarding the municipality's opinions, yesterday (14th) submitted eleven articles in writing to Fessenden, the consultant of the Municipal Council, regarding what needs to be improved in the municipal administration, which are very important for the future prosperity of Shanghai. We will now explore and disclose the contents of the letter:

To Mr. Fessenden: Since you came to Shanghai to take the position of consultant for the Municipal Council of the Public Concession, the Chinese society has believed that this move is a plan to extend the life of the Public Concession and hinder the early completion of our country's movement for unified sovereignty. After reading the documents you have published with the Municipal Council, although we slightly understand your position, we are still skeptical and have not been relieved. This is evidenced by the Municipal Council's notice soliciting opinions from Chinese organizations and individuals, which has been published for almost a month, but few have responded. The reason for this is worth pondering deeply. Now, we have been informed by the Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association that you have entrusted them with soliciting opinions, and we have learned that publishing the notice to solicit Chinese opinions is not just a formality, but seems to be a sincere sign of acceptance, then the Chamber, which represents all the shops in Shanghai, cannot remain silent and tell you. However, since the scope of what you want to solicit has not been specified, the Chamber will also present the general opinions of all its members for your consideration. (A) Immediately and unconditionally completely recover the concession, is the common aspiration of our people. (B) Before the concession is recovered, the administration of the Shanghai Public Concession should be improved. The details are as follows: (1) The political power of the concession municipality is only controlled by foreigners who make up a very small percentage of the population. The Chinese residents, who make up more than 95 percent of the population, do not have equal participation rights. This should be improved. (2) The municipal legislative body is extremely incomplete, because the annual Western ratepayers only hold a meeting once a year, similar to a city council meeting, with a time limit of at most three hours. It is difficult to have a detailed discussion of the annual municipal report, budget and final accounts, and citizen development plans. The Chamber believes that a standing city council should be established in the future to preside over municipal legislative matters. Chinese and foreign taxpayers should each elect a number of councilors in proportion to the amount of taxes paid to organize it, and hold meetings several times a year, so that municipal legislation has considerable completeness. The Board of Directors of the Municipal Council is only an executive committee and has no say in legislative matters. This should be improved. (3) Before the establishment of a standing city council, all annual reports, budgets, final accounts, and various proposals submitted to the annual meeting of Western ratepayers should also be submitted to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association for discussion, in accordance with law and reason. This should be improved. (4) The number of seats on the Board of Directors of the Municipal Council is not proportional to the population, but should at least be proportional to the amount of taxes paid. Although the current three Chinese directors will soon be increased to five, it is still far from proportional to the amount of taxes. To put it another way, only according to the memorandum issued by the Municipal Council on July 18, 1927 (in fact, taxes paid by Chinese residents but paid by foreigners on their behalf are not included), the total tax amount paid by Chinese residents accounts for 55 percent, and foreigners account for 45 percent. The ratio of Chinese directors to foreign directors should be eleven to nine. This should be improved. (5) All senior officials of the Municipal Council are foreigners. Economically, the increased expenditure on salaries, allowances, and travel expenses increases the burden on taxpayers. Administratively, the differences in language, writing, customs, and habits increase many inconveniences and barriers. In the future, Chinese residents should be hired to serve as senior officials, and Chinese residents should be used to record various documents, reports, official letters, and notices, so that the economy can be saved and administrative barriers can be removed. This should be improved. (6) The staff of the Municipal Council are now using the above-mentioned barriers to create many malpractices, such as the fire brigade taking advantage of fires to loot, the engineering department making things difficult and picky, the health department being hypercritical, and the police department sheltering and oppressing people. The reason for this is nothing more than seeking money. If they are reported to higher authorities, they are all dismissed for lack of evidence. To eliminate accumulated abuses, Chinese residents must be employed as senior officials to facilitate communication between superiors and subordinates, and the staff must be strictly trained. This should be improved. (7) The Municipal Council's expenses are actually used inappropriately, such as building many roads outside the concession, which only increases the resentment of Chinese residents and results in the disrepair and ruggedness of roads within the concession. This should be improved. (8) In terms of public security, according to records in the newspapers, Shanghai ranks first in terms of kidnapping and theft cases, and the distribution of police officers is often uneven. In the future, special attention should be paid to police affairs, and gambling institutions that create sources of crime, such as dog racing tracks, and late-night entertainment venues, such as dance halls, should be prohibited. It is especially important to cooperate closely with the Municipal Public Security Bureau and the French Concession to unify defense, so that criminals have no escape and the police do not shirk responsibility from each other. This should be improved. (9) The Municipal Council does not pay enough attention to Chinese education. Judging from the budget, Chinese education expenses only account for one-thirty-second of the total education expenses. In terms of population, the number of Chinese children's schools is too small, and the management of the four Chinese children's public schools is in the hands of foreigners, and there are many barriers to children's psychology and writing applications. The books in the library are all in Western languages, which makes it impossible for Chinese residents to read Chinese books. Furthermore, the establishment of three Chinese children's primary schools was decided in the previous year, but the western district has not yet opened, and the promotion and expansion have been ignored. Only one-fourth of the funds required for the construction of the two planned school buildings are listed in this year's budget. In the future, Chinese education expenses should be specially expanded. Chinese education expenses should account for at least 20 percent of the Municipal Council's annual income, in order to popularize primary education and improve citizens' knowledge. Chinese education should be unified and managed by the Chinese Education Department, and all principals and teachers, except for foreign language teachers, should be Chinese residents. This should be improved. (10) The sanitation facilities in the concession are extremely incomplete for Chinese residents. For example, in terms of hospitals, although the Chinese population is over 800,000, there are few hospitals, while Westerners have many conveniences. This should be improved. (11) The municipal administration of the concession is superficially impressive, but its content is far from modern municipal administration and can be said to be incomplete. For example, the household registration is neither strictly investigated nor statistically detailed, so that kidnappers and thieves mostly use the concession as their lair. This should be improved. The above articles are only the most important ones that are specifically presented to you for consideration. As for the commendable aspects of the Municipal Council's facilities, but for those who are progressing with the times, all facilities should progress with the times. If they stick to the old ways and ignore the wishes of Chinese residents and do not adopt the world's newest systems, not only will cooperation be difficult to achieve, but all prosperity will not be able to increase, and the existing prosperity may be lost and become an outdated market. Because we believe that you have no preconceived notions, we present general opinions for your consideration and hope that you will investigate and act accordingly.

Yesterday's Hearing on Labor-Management Dispute in the Pharmaceutical Industry

Since the pharmaceutical workers announced their strike, it has been the second day. Labor and management are refuting each other, with very resolute attitudes. All stores in the concession are closed, and slogans are plastered on the walls. The workers went to the municipal government to petition the day before yesterday afternoon. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, they convened a general meeting of members in the concession area and went to the Social Affairs Bureau of the municipal party headquarters to petition. It is said that the Social Affairs Bureau has agreed to convene a mediation meeting this afternoon. The opinions of party and government agencies on the industry dispute are supplemented as follows:

Talks at the Municipal Party Committee: Since the launch of the issue of placing unemployed workers, labor and management have refused to yield to each other and have published statements in newspapers one after another. It is difficult for outsiders to understand the merits of the matter. A reporter from the National Society visited a member of the Civil Training Committee of the Municipal Party Committee to inquire about the truth. The following is an excerpt of the conversation. The committee member said that the unemployment problem is of great importance and depends entirely on the proper handling by party and government agencies to prevent it from becoming a catastrophe. If party and government agencies turn a blind eye to the unemployed workers' pleas for food, it would not only be contrary to the party's aim of helping workers, but also easily lead to social unrest due to the increase of vagrants. The reason why Chinese society is unstable today is not unrelated to the failure to solve the unemployment problem. Therefore, for the sake of social stability, we sincerely hope that party and government agencies can properly solve the unemployment problem. However, before solving this problem, two points should be noted: (1) The character and ability of the unemployed should be strictly examined. Those who are kind should be placed, and bad elements should be given severance pay and dismissed immediately. (2) The financial ability of the employer should also be investigated in detail. If the financial resources are insufficient and the employer is forced to place workers, it would be like swallowing something whole without chewing, and it will not stop until both sides are hurt. However, if the employer has strong capital and a prosperous business, but does not pay attention to the unemployment problem and refuses to accept placement in defiance of the orders of party and government agencies, then the party and government agencies should severely punish them to deter troublemakers. The party's policy on agricultural and industrial issues is to develop Chinese industry on the one hand and to safeguard the lives of workers on the other. The party wants to safeguard the lives of workers under the conditions of developing Chinese industry. At the same time, it wants to develop Chinese industry under the conditions of safeguarding the lives of workers. We certainly do not allow the labor side to destroy industry in order to maintain their livelihood, but we also do not allow the employer side to destroy workers in the name of industry. This is a very clear principle. This time, the Municipal Party Committee is also proceeding with this principle in the issue of placing unemployed workers in the pharmaceutical industry. Because the pharmaceutical workers' union was once controlled and manipulated by communists, strikes and work slowdowns occurred from time to time, and both labor and management suffered from it. Later, after the efforts of this party department to reorganize it, the communist trade union was completely abolished and the current trade union was established to carry out work under the leadership of this party. However, the employer, believing that the workers were kind and could be deceived, repeatedly launched attacks and dismissed a large number of workers. The Municipal Party Committee was deeply concerned that bad elements might be mixed in among them. Last year, it joined the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau in conducting a detailed review of the unemployed workers. As of recently, more than 130 people were found to be kind people and were planned to be placed separately. The second step was to start investigating the employer's business status and financial ability. Among the more than 300 pharmacies in this city, it was found that more than 40 pharmacies had developed businesses and earned a net profit of more than 10,000 yuan last year, such as Hu Qingyutang and Hanchun, which each earned more than 200,000 yuan. This time, the pharmaceutical workers' union is placing unemployed workers in these 40 pharmacies, allocating them according to their financial strength, roughly one person for every 10,000 yuan earned. After the pharmaceutical workers' union completed its preparations, it requested the Municipal Party Committee to convene a meeting of labor and management to discuss the issue of placement. The Municipal Party Committee immediately notified both parties to convene a meeting on a fixed date, but the employer refused to attend, making it impossible to talk. On March 8, the Municipal Party Committee again ordered the employer to find a way to place the workers, but the employer ignored it. Therefore, the trade union had to take direct action, sending the qualified unemployed workers to various stores to request placement. However, the Pharmaceutical Merchants Association not only refused to accept them, but also ordered each store to hire police to demonstrate and intimidate. Currently, the Chinese-administered area has largely accommodated them, and Tie Daqiao and Qingyutang in the concession area have also agreed to accept them. However, the employer of Hu Qingyutang actually used the Communist Party, and the Communist Party also colluded with capitalists to distribute reactionary leaflets under false pretenses, undermining the placement plan. It has now been found that Ru Shenxiu and Ye Zengyuan of Chuanrongtang are their leaders and will be sent to military and police agencies for arrest and prosecution. As for the employer's side, they are purely blinded by Zhang Meian and a few others. The Pharmaceutical Merchants Association is controlled by Zhang. The Municipal Party Committee will also issue a warning to them, it is said.

Municipal Government Approval: Shanghai Special Municipal Government Approval (No. 690) The original submitter is the Pharmaceutical Branch, submitting a case stating that the trade union is forcibly placing workers and disturbing the store's business, requesting that an order be issued to stop it. All the submissions are noted. If the trade union has any excessive actions, it is inappropriate. In addition to instructing the Social Affairs and Public Security Bureaus to investigate and properly stop it, the branch should still instruct the employer to abide by the approved method and handle it properly to resolve the dispute. Let it be known. This approval, attachments are stored. March 11, Republic of China Year 19, Mayor Zhang.

Yesterday's General Membership Meeting of the Xiangchang Cotton Weaving Workers' Union

The Xiangchang Cotton Weaving Workers' Union held a general membership meeting at the assembly hall of the General Labor Union yesterday at 2:00 PM. Over 280 members attended. The presidium consisted of Zhao Peirong, He Xiaolian, and Wu Baoshan. Gu Rongxi was the secretary. Xu Yefu of the Municipal Civil Training Committee and Comrade Wu Zhen of the Second District Party Department attended and provided guidance. Matters resolved: (1) Each member of each association shall pay two yuan to be kept by two people from each group as funeral donation for Xing Youcheng. (2) Female workers No. 3 and No. 24, who left the association without cause before the tragedy, shall each be fined five yuan to fund the Xing Youcheng memorial service. (3) Comrade Zhao, the secretary of the association, has worked hard and shall be given a subsidy of 70 yuan to show preferential treatment. (4) All workers may only leave the workshop and completely sever ties with the factory after the issues of death, injury compensation, and medical expenses have been resolved. (5) Li Lantai, He Xiaolian, Zhu Changgui, Li Lianfu, Jiang Bifu, Zhao Peirong, and Han Detai were elected as the seven plenipotentiary representatives of the association to keep all the union documents and handle the case as soon as possible. (6) Request the municipal government to negotiate with the French Concession authorities to punish the murderers and compensate for the losses to comfort the spirits. (7) Request the government to investigate and prosecute Detective Cheng, the French detective who led the French police to kill the workers, and Shi, who instigated the crime. (8) Notify the public of the entire city to condemn the act. (9) Prepare for the Xing Youcheng memorial service, which shall be the responsibility of the union representatives. The venue shall be borrowed from the General Labor Union, and the expenses shall be allocated from Xing Youcheng's severance pay and the fines from female worker Zhou Xiaomei No. 3. (10) Request the Social Affairs Bureau to approve the negotiation with the police within three days to recover Xing Youcheng's body, put it in a coffin, and bury it in the No. 130 public cemetery. (11) Request the Preparatory Committee of the Municipal General Labor Union to transfer the request to the Municipal Civil Training Committee to order the Social Affairs Bureau to allow the Xiangchang Workers' Union to exercise its powers and continue to handle the tragedy in accordance with the resolutions of the general meeting until the case is completely resolved. (12) Death, injury compensation, medical expenses, and funeral expenses have already been requested from the Municipal Civil Training Committee and the Social Affairs Bureau for handling. Starting today, the Social Affairs Bureau is requested to bring it up for negotiation with the employer. (13) Shout slogans. (14) Adjourn the meeting.

The Arbitration Committee Rules on the Samsung Factory Case

Factory 1 is Allowed to Close

Factory 2 Continues to Operate as Before

The Shanghai Special Municipal Labor-Management Arbitration Committee ruled that the Samsung Cotton and Iron Factory No. 1 is allowed to close. The employer should try to retain all child laborers and students at Factory 1. In addition, they should give severance pay to other workers in accordance with the interim measures of the city's workers' retirement benefits. Factory 2 should continue to operate as before. All requests from the employer to reduce workers are rejected.

Shanghai, 14th (Dentsu News Agency) The Dornier aircraft for the second experimental flight between Shanghai and Fukuoka took off from Fukuoka at 8:24 AM this morning (9:20 AM Japan time). It fought against headwinds, making navigation very difficult. It finally arrived safely in Shanghai at 3:45 PM, taking a time of six hours and twenty-one minutes.

Forced Removal of Shanties in the Wusong Fortress Area

In the vicinity of the Wusong Fort Taiwan, on public land, there are general migrants from other provinces who have built grass shacks and lived there. Deng Zhenquan, the commander of the Wusong Fortress, believes that the area within three or four miles is the defense flood land of the north and south fortresses of the fortress, and he fears that bandits will use these shanties to cause trouble, which is related to defense affairs. Therefore, he issued a notice a few days ago, ordering all shanties to be demolished and moved out of the area within five days. As for the residents of private land in the Fan area, they must also comply with this deadline and report the names, ages, occupations, and number of people of both men and women. Details have been recorded in the newspaper on the 9th. It is now known that the five-day deadline expired the day before yesterday. Of the two or three hundred shanties on the public land, about thirty have complied with the deadline and demolished them. Most are still watching and have taken no action. Yesterday was the first day after the deadline. The command saw that the general shanties were resisting demolition, so it sent troops yesterday to enforce the orders on those who disobeyed, causing most of those who demolished to move to Baoshan.

Shanghai-Chengdu Aviation to Build Aircraft Station

Simultaneously Building the Shanghai Management Branch

Nie Kaiyi, the director of the Shanghai-Chengdu Aviation Management Office, reported that the Shanghai Management Branch was too far from the Hongqiao Airport, and that the delivery of mail took time and wasted a lot of time. He specially requested and was approved by the Ministry of Communications to build a large aircraft station at Hongqiao, and at the same time move the Shanghai Branch of the Management Office into the station. It was contracted by the Shengtailou Construction Company of this city yesterday, and construction will begin soon, with the aim of completing it by the end of May.

Only One Guild Allowed for the Same Industry in the Same District

Central Training Department Orders Revision

The Commercial Reorganization Committee Strictly Enforces the Order

The Shanghai Special Municipal Commercial Reorganization Committee previously stipulated in the Law on Industrial and Commercial Guilds that only one guild should be established for the same industry in the same area. All industries in this city that have more than one organization should be merged in accordance with the law. However, the national systems of various industries are often organized separately due to customary relations and the division of importance in business. For example, in the same silk industry, there are the Qianjiang Guild Hall, the Zhejiang Huzhou Crepe Industry Association, the Shandong Henan Silk Industry Association, the Shengjing Guild Hall, and the Hangzhou Silk Industry Association. In fact, the members of each group are all silk merchants and should not be divided into separate organizations. However, given the historical and customary relations, the Commercial Reorganization Committee, in order to take the facts into consideration, originally intended to still allow them to be grouped separately. Therefore, in Article 1 of the organizational and reorganization procedures, in addition to limiting the establishment of one guild for the same industry in the same area, it added a proviso: "However, those that differ in the nature of their affairs in terms of importance do not have to be forced to form a single organization, and their names and scope shall be determined." In addition, Item 4, on merging in accordance with the law, added, "However, if there are indeed places where it is impossible to merge due to customary history or the nature of the business, it may be changed as appropriate after verification." The association submitted this procedure to the Central Committee for filing. Yesterday, it received Instruction No. 2087 from the Training Department of the Central Party Headquarters, stating that the submission and attachments had been received. Upon investigation of the various laws and regulations submitted by the association, the alternative measures for industrial and commercial guild reorganization and the organizational procedures passed by the association's standing committee, Article 1 and Article 4, regarding the joint organization and merger of the same industry, are not based on any laws promulgated by the Central Government and should be deleted and revised to comply with the filing requested by the law. The association has followed the order and deleted the alternative measures and provisos added to Article 1 and Article 4 of the procedure after deliberation by the plenary meeting, and has handed them over to the guidance department for strict implementation of the same industry merger measures.

The Silk Industry Branch's Termination is Imminent

The Silk Industry Branch of the Commercial and Civil Association recently received a letter from the Shanghai Special Municipal Merchant Group Reorganization Committee, ordering it to merge and reorganize with other silk industry groups and to report 11 representatives within 10 days for review and commissioning, together with representatives from other industry groups, to form the Shanghai Special Municipal Silk Industry Group Reorganization Committee to handle the merger and reorganization procedures, etc. On the 3rd of this month, the Executive Committee was convened to discuss and resolve to comply with the order to nominate 11 representatives including Wang Yansong and Shen Qinzai, and report them to the Commercial Reorganization Committee for review and commissioning. It is now heard that the association is rushing to handle the closing matters in order to hand over, and other association affairs have been suspended temporarily, waiting for the takeover.

Continued News on the Pacific Shipping Tide

Tramp Ships Disrupting Cargo Transportation Along the Pacific Route: Since the incident of Japanese ships arbitrarily lowering freight rates, almost all shipping companies within the association have suffered significant losses in this time of low cargo volume and many ships. Shipping companies that have not joined the association have recently joined this competitive battle, further reducing freight rates for goods shipped to the United States, even lower than the association's set prices, and offering rebates. Recently, various tramp ships have even cancelled lighterage fees to solicit cargo from the Yangtze River and the Northern and Southern Seas bound for the United States, causing a sharp decline in the export business of postal ships. The association has no solution for this, and the Sino-American freight transportation has become chaotic.

Japanese Ships Reduce Passenger Ticket Prices: The Japanese Osaka Company in this city has six ships specially dispatched in the Pacific, on the Shanghai-Seattle line. Since last month, Nippon Yusen Kaisha (NYK Line) has transferred the 22,000-ton Siberia Maru to this route and added new ships, Binglu Chuanmaru and Hiedamaru. Osaka Line has suffered an invisible blow in the passenger business. Recently, due to the lack of export cargo in Shanghai, it has decided not to send ships for fifty days. It is now heard that the company has decided to reduce the price of tickets from Shanghai to the United States, selling first-class cabins for only 180 yen, starting from April 1, in order to compete.

Stranded Japanese Ship's Cargo Discharged: The US-China postal ship Al Baham, of the Osaka Company, carrying a large quantity of salted fish and cotton from the United States to Shanghai, ran aground outside Yokohama. The bottom of the ship was trapped by reefs. The company sent a ship to tow it, but to no avail. The Shanghai cargo on board was first discharged and transported to Shanghai. Passengers from the United States to Shanghai also transferred to NYK ships to Shanghai. The ship is still being salvaged. Because the ship's hull has been damaged, even if it is towed out, it will have to be docked for major repairs.

For the convenience of connecting trains and travelers on the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways, the Traffic Department of the two railways plans to make slight changes to the current train timetables. Local News Two

[P Counterfeit Money Case Judgment>

Lu Li Shi Sentenced to Three Years

Remaining Offenders Sentenced to Two Years and One Year

Qian Yumin, a detective from the French Concession Police, recently discovered that Lu Li Shi, aka Zhang Li Shi, a woman from Zhenjiang with a registration number of 42 Xicheng Li, Ma Lang Road, was privately setting up a counterfeit money machine and sending people out to use it. He immediately reported to the West Detective Chief and quietly went to the woman's home and seized more than 300 counterfeit five-yuan banknotes of the Central Bank, 20 counterfeit banknotes of the Bank of China, and 15 counterfeit banknotes of the Bank of Communications, totaling more than 300 yuan, and took them to the police station. Subsequently, Wang Guisheng, Ma Songshan, Li Youming, Cui Zhensheng, and related persons Chen Xide and Cao Ruicheng were arrested for assisting in the use of the counterfeit money, and the value of the counterfeit money seized was brought back to the police station together. Yesterday, they were jointly sent to the French Court for investigation. Detective Qian first reported the previous situation and presented the counterfeit money to the court. When questioned, Lu Li Shi claimed that the counterfeit money was sent by Liang Qingshan, who was on the run, and that she was unaware that it was counterfeit money. The remaining words were vague. When questioned, Wang Guisheng, Ma Songshan, Li Youming, and Cui Zhensheng all confessed that the counterfeit money was actually given to them by Hu Jinshan and Liang Qingsan, who were on the run, for use, with a charge of two yuan and four corners per ten yuan. Chen Xide and Cao Ruicheng confessed that they had gone to Ma Songshan's house to visit a few days ago and were mistakenly arrested. They knew nothing about the use of counterfeit money and asked for investigation. The Chinese and Western officials judged that the defendants were indeed guilty of violating Article 211 of the Criminal Law, ordering Lu Li Shi to be imprisoned in the women's prison for three years, Wang Guisheng and Ma Songshan to be imprisoned for two years each, and Li Youming and Cui Zhensheng to be imprisoned for one year each. Upon completion of their sentences, they will all be permanently expelled from the concession. Chen Xide and Cao Ruicheng will be deported. The seized counterfeit money will be destroyed.

Two People Sentenced to Death in the Kidnapping Case of Qu Chengqing

Remaining Offenders Sentenced to Imprisonment Separately

Qu Chengqing, a clerk at Tienshen Foreign Firm, was kidnapped at midnight on January 11 from the back door of his residence at 1760 Haining Road and hidden in a bandit's den at 1458 East Westward Road. The Jinghui Mountain Police detectives learned of this, rescued Qu, and arrested 11 male and female bandits. They were repeatedly sent to the Provisional Court for final investigation. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu opened the court and announced the death sentences for Zhang Zhangji and Wang Qieneng. He Qing'en, Wang Yuqing, Wang Afu, and Shen Adi were sentenced to life imprisonment. Guan Kangsong was sentenced to 17 years of imprisonment, and Xu Asan was sentenced to 12 years of imprisonment. Chen Shizhong, Lou Zhushi, and Gu Yangshi were all found not guilty. The seized pistols, bullets, handcuffs, and other items were confiscated. It is said that He Qing'en, one of the convicts sentenced, was a dismissed detective from the Public Concession Police.

Liu Arong, Who Kidnapped People for Ransom, Sentenced to Death

Ma Zonglai, a patrol detective from the Xinzha Police Station, previously arrested Liu Arong, a bandit from Jiangbei who was wanted for kidnapping Zhou Zongzhi for ransom. He was sent to the Provisional Court, where he was interrogated and sentenced to life imprisonment. Later, Liu refused to accept the judgment and filed an appeal, which was rejected. Under the review of the Provincial Government, it was found that there were still problems with the sentencing of the crime, and it was sent back for retrial. The Court of Appeal completed the retrial yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, with Judge Qiu and Assessors Wu and Li presiding over the Court of Appeal, announcing that Liu Arong was sentenced to death for the crime of kidnapping people for ransom.

The Missing Steamer Returned to Wusong Yesterday

Two Fishing Boats Helped to Escape Danger

Regarding the incident of the Wan Shun steamer of the Hubei South Lida Company being missing, as reported in yesterday's newspaper, it is now learned that the steamer sailed back to Wusong yesterday morning. However, according to the helmsman of the steamer, although no disaster occurred in this sudden storm, the danger was extreme. When the squall suddenly broke out that day, the steamer was on the Yangmian River upstream of Yawawo Sand. Due to the surge of wind and waves, the steamer lost its ability to sail. At the critical moment, it was fortunate to encounter two fishing boats from Yawawo Sand, which guided the steamer into a small port in Yawawo Sand to avoid the wind and waves. With the help of the two fishing boats, a iron anchor was lost from the fishing boat and a railing wood was destroyed. When the steamer sailed into the small port, the fire on the ship had been cut off. The fishing boat, feeling sorry for the plight of the ship being caught in a storm, lent food and used it in small quantities. When the helmsman spoke, he was overjoyed and expressed his deep gratitude to the fishing boat. It has now returned to Song without loss, which is indeed a great fortune amidst misfortune. The steamer has sailed to Shanghai. According to the information reported to the owner, Mr. Lin plans to compensate the fishing boat for the lost iron anchor and railing wood, and to express his gratitude for the deep kindness of rescue.

At 10:00 AM the day before yesterday, a man suddenly fell to the ground at the intersection of Baker Road and Xinzha Road.
